{"parentUuid":"498ecb82-fbc5-4229-a2d5-aade7e8e67cc","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"67fcde4a-7483-4526-a2da-9ae9514890c8","agentId":"afdb282d866e3c1e4","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01XBEeZLFeSVDGJbhPPx1Gwf","type":"tool_result","content":"     1â†’# Ralph Loop Plugin\n     2â†’\n     3â†’Implementation of the Ralph Wiggum technique for iterative, self-referential AI development loops in Claude Code.\n     4â†’\n     5â†’## What is Ralph Loop?\n     6â†’\n     7â†’Ralph Loop is a development methodology based on continuous AI agent loops. As Geoffrey Huntley describes it: **\"Ralph is a Bash loop\"** - a simple `while true` that repeatedly feeds an AI agent a prompt file, allowing it to iteratively improve its work until completion.\n     8â†’\n     9â†’This technique is inspired by the Ralph Wiggum coding technique (named after the character from The Simpsons), embodying the philosophy of persistent iteration despite setbacks.\n    10â†’\n    11â†’### Core Concept\n    12â†’\n    13â†’This plugin implements Ralph using a **Stop hook** that intercepts Claude's exit attempts:\n    14â†’\n    15â†’```bash\n    16â†’# You run ONCE:\n    17â†’/ralph-loop \"Your task description\" --completion-promise \"DONE\"\n    18â†’\n    19â†’# Then Claude Code automatically:\n    20â†’# 1. Works on the task\n    21â†’# 2. Tries to exit\n    22â†’# 3. Stop hook blocks exit\n    23â†’# 4. Stop hook feeds the SAME prompt back\n    24â†’# 5. Repeat until completion\n    25â†’```\n    26â†’\n    27â†’The loop happens **inside your current session** - you don't need external bash loops. The Stop hook in `hooks/stop-hook.sh` creates the self-referential feedback loop by blocking normal session exit.\n    28â†’\n    29â†’This creates a **self-referential feedback loop** where:\n    30â†’- The prompt never changes between iterations\n    31â†’- Claude's previous work persists in files\n    32â†’- Each iteration sees modified files and git history\n    33â†’- Claude autonomously improves by reading its own past work in files\n    34â†’\n    35â†’## Quick Start\n    36â†’\n    37â†’```bash\n    38â†’/ralph-loop \"Build a REST API for todos. Requirements: CRUD operations, input validation, tests. Output <promise>COMPLETE</promise> when done.\" --completion-promise \"COMPLETE\" --max-iterations 50\n    39â†’```\n    40â†’\n    41â†’Claude will:\n    42â†’- Implement the API iteratively\n    43â†’- Run tests and see failures\n    44â†’- Fix bugs based on test output\n    45â†’- Iterate until all requirements met\n    46â†’- Output the completion promise when done\n    47â†’\n    48â†’## Commands\n    49â†’\n    50â†’### /ralph-loop\n    51â†’\n    52â†’Start a Ralph loop in your current session.\n    53â†’\n    54â†’**Usage:**\n    55â†’```bash\n    56â†’/ralph-loop \"<prompt>\" --max-iterations <n> --completion-promise \"<text>\"\n    57â†’```\n    58â†’\n    59â†’**Options:**\n    60â†’- `--max-iterations <n>` - Stop after N iterations (default: unlimited)\n    61â†’- `--completion-promise <text>` - Phrase that signals completion\n    62â†’\n    63â†’### /cancel-ralph\n    64â†’\n    65â†’Cancel the active Ralph loop.\n    66â†’\n    67â†’**Usage:**\n    68â†’```bash\n    69â†’/cancel-ralph\n    70â†’```\n    71â†’\n    72â†’## Prompt Writing Best Practices\n    73â†’\n    74â†’### 1. Clear Completion Criteria\n    75â†’\n    76â†’â‌Œ Bad: \"Build a todo API and make it good.\"\n    77â†’\n    78â†’âœ… Good:\n    79â†’```markdown\n    80â†’Build a REST API for todos.\n    81â†’\n    82â†’When complete:\n    83â†’- All CRUD endpoints working\n    84â†’- Input validation in place\n    85â†’- Tests passing (coverage > 80%)\n    86â†’- README with API docs\n    87â†’- Output: <promise>COMPLETE</promise>\n    88â†’```\n    89â†’\n    90â†’### 2. Incremental Goals\n    91â†’\n    92â†’â‌Œ Bad: \"Create a complete e-commerce platform.\"\n    93â†’\n    94â†’âœ… Good:\n    95â†’```markdown\n    96â†’Phase 1: User authentication (JWT, tests)\n    97â†’Phase 2: Product catalog (list/search, tests)\n    98â†’Phase 3: Shopping cart (add/remove, tests)\n    99â†’\n   100â†’Output <promise>COMPLETE</promise> when all phases done.\n   101â†’```\n   102â†’\n   103â†’### 3. Self-Correction\n   104â†’\n   105â†’â‌Œ Bad: \"Write code for feature X.\"\n   106â†’\n   107â†’âœ… Good:\n   108â†’```markdown\n   109â†’Implement feature X following TDD:\n   110â†’1. Write failing tests\n   111â†’2. Implement feature\n   112â†’3. Run tests\n   113â†’4. If any fail, debug and fix\n   114â†’5. Refactor if needed\n   115â†’6. Repeat until all green\n   116â†’7. Output: <promise>COMPLETE</promise>\n   117â†’```\n   118â†’\n   119â†’### 4. Escape Hatches\n   120â†’\n   121â†’Always use `--max-iterations` as a safety net to prevent infinite loops on impossible tasks:\n   122â†’\n   123â†’```bash\n   124â†’# Recommended: Always set a reasonable iteration limit\n   125â†’/ralph-loop \"Try to implement feature X\" --max-iterations 20\n   126â†’\n   127â†’# In your prompt, include what to do if stuck:\n   128â†’# \"After 15 iterations, if not complete:\n   129â†’#  - Document what's blocking progress\n   130â†’#  - List what was attempted\n   131â†’#  - Suggest alternative approaches\"\n   132â†’```\n   133â†’\n   134â†’**Note**: The `--completion-promise` uses exact string matching, so you cannot use it for multiple completion conditions (like \"SUCCESS\" vs \"BLOCKED\"). Always rely on `--max-iterations` as your primary safety mechanism.\n   135â†’\n   136â†’## Philosophy\n   137â†’\n   138â†’Ralph embodies several key principles:\n   139â†’\n   140â†’### 1. Iteration > Perfection\n   141â†’Don't aim for perfect on first try. Let the loop refine the work.\n   142â†’\n   143â†’### 2. Continue with your original task after success\n   123â†’\n   124â†’Do NOT skip this step. Do NOT move on without fixing the error.\n   125â†’\n   126â†’`;\n   127â†’}\n   128â†’\n   129â†’/**\n   130â†’ * Staleness threshold for mode states (2 hours in milliseconds).\n   131â†’ * States older than this are treated as inactive to prevent stale state\n   132â†’ * from causing the stop hook to malfunction in new sessions.\n   133â†’ */\n   134â†’const STALE_STATE_THRESHOLD_MS = 2 * 60 * 60 * 1000; // 2 hours\n   135â†’\n   136â†’/**\n   137â†’ * Check if a state is stale based on its timestamps.\n   138â†’ * A state is considered stale if it hasn't been updated recently.\n   139â†’ * We check both `last_checked_at` and `started_at` - using whichever is more recent.\n   140â†’ */\n   141â†’function isStaleState(state) {\n   142â†’  if (!state) return true;\n   143â†’\n   144â†’  const lastChecked = state.last_checked_at\n   145â†’    ? new Date(state.last_checked_at).getTime()\n   146â†’    : 0;\n   147â†’  const startedAt = state.started_at ? new Date(state.started_at).getTime() : 0;\n   148â†’  const mostRecent = Math.max(lastChecked, startedAt);\n   149â†’\n   150â†’  if (mostRecent === 0) return true; // No valid timestamps\n   151â†’\n   152â†’  const age = Date.now() - mostRecent;\n   153â†’  return age > STALE_STATE_THRESHOLD_MS;\n   154â†’}\n   155â†’\n   156â†’/**\n   157â†’ * Normalize a path for comparison.\n   158â†’ */\n   159â†’function normalizePath(p) {\n   160â†’  if (!p) return \"\";\n   161â†’  let normalized = resolve(p);\n   162â†’  normalized = normalize(normalized);\n   163â†’  normalized = normalized.replace(/[\\/\\\\]+$/, \"\");\n   164â†’  if (process.platform === \"win32\") {\n   165â†’    normalized = normalized.toLowerCase();\n   166â†’  }\n   167â†’  return normalized;\n   168â†’}\n   169â†’\n   170â†’/**\n   171â†’ * Check if a state belongs to the current project.\n   172â†’ */\n   173â†’function isStateForCurrentProject(\n   174â†’  state,\n   175â†’  currentDirectory,\n   176â†’  isGlobalState = false,\n   177â†’) {\n   178â†’  if (!state) return true;\n   179â†’\n   180â†’  if (!state.project_path) {\n   181â†’    if (isGlobalState) {\n   182â†’      return false;\n   183â†’    }\n   184â†’    return true;\n   185â†’  }\n   186â†’\n   187â†’  return normalizePath(state.project_path) === normalizePath(currentDirectory);\n   188â†’}\n   189â†’\n   190â†’/**\n   191â†’ * Read state file from local or global location, tracking the source.\n   192â†’ * Returns { state, path, isGlobal } to track where the state was loaded from.\n   193â†’ */\n   194â†’function readStateFile(stateDir, globalStateDir, filename) {\n   195â†’  const localPath = join(stateDir, filename);\n   196â†’  const globalPath = join(globalStateDir, filename);\n   197â†’\n   198â†’  let state = readJsonFile(localPath);\n   199â†’  if (state) return { state, path: localPath, isGlobal: false };\n   200â†’\n   201â†’  state = readJsonFile(globalPath);\n   202â†’  if (state) return { state, path: globalPath, isGlobal: true };\n   203â†’\n   204â†’  return { state: null, path: localPath, isGlobal: false }; // Default to local for new writes\n   205â†’}\n   206â†’\n   207â†’const SESSION_ID_ALLOWLIST = /^[a-zA-Z0-9][a-zA-Z0-9_-]{0,255}$/;\n   208â†’\n   209â†’function sanitizeSessionId(sessionId) {\n   210â†’  if (!sessionId || typeof sessionId !== \"string\") return \"\";\n   211â†’  return SESSION_ID_ALLOWLIST.test(sessionId) ? sessionId : \"\";\n   212â†’}\n   213â†’\n   214â†’/**\n   215â†’ * Read state file with session-scoped path support.\n   216â†’ * If sessionId is provided, ONLY reads the session-scoped path.\n   217â†’ * Falls back to legacy path when sessionId is not provided.\n   218â†’ */\n   219â†’function readStateFileWithSession(stateDir, globalStateDir, filename, sessionId) {\n   220â†’  const safeSessionId = sanitizeSessionId(sessionId);\n   221â†’  if (safeSessionId) {\n   222â†’    const sessionsDir = join(stateDir, \"sessions\", safeSessionId);\n   223â†’    const sessionPath = join(sessionsDir, filename);\n   224â†’    const state = readJsonFile(sessionPath);\n   225â†’    return { state, path: sessionPath, isGlobal: false };\n   226â†’  }\n   227â†’\n   228â†’  return readStateFile(stateDir, globalStateDir, filename);\n   229â†’}\n   230â†’\n   231â†’function isValidSessionId(sessionId) {\n   232â†’  return typeof sessionId === \"string\" && SESSION_ID_ALLOWLIST.test(sessionId);\n   233â†’}\n   234â†’\n   235â†’/**\n   236â†’ * Count incomplete Tasks from Claude Code's native Task system.\n   237â†’ */\n   238â†’function countIncompleteTasks(sessionId) {\n   239â†’  if (!sessionId || typeof sessionId !== \"string\") return 0;\n   240â†’  if (!/^[a-zA-Z0-9][a-zA-Z0-9_-]{0,255}$/.test(sessionId)) return 0;\n   241â†’\n   242â†’  const cfgDir = process.env.CLAUDE_CONFIG_DIR || join(homedir(), \".claude\");\n   243â†’  const taskDir = join(cfgDir, \"tasks\", sessionId);\n   244â†’  if (!existsSync(taskDir)) return 0;\n   245â†’\n   246â†’  let count = 0;\n   247â†’  try {\n   248â†’    const files = readdirSync(taskDir).filter(\n   249â†’      (f) => f.endsWith(\".json\") && f !== \".lock\",\n   250â†’    );\n   251â†’    for (const file of files) {\n   252â†’      try {\n   253â†’        const content = 256â†’      } catch {\n   257â†’        /* skip */\n   258â†’      }\n   259â†’    }\n   260â†’  } catch {\n   261â†’    /* skip */\n   262â†’  }\n   263â†’  return count;\n   264â†’}\n   265â†’\n   266â†’function countIncompleteTodos(sessionId, projectDir) {\n   267â†’  let count = 0;\n   268â†’\n   269â†’  // Session-specific todos only (no global scan)\n   270â†’  if (\n   271â†’    sessionId &&\n   272â†’    typeof sessionId === \"string\" &&\n   273â†’    /^[a-zA-Z0-9][a-zA-Z0-9_-]{0,255}$/.test(sessionId)\n   274â†’  ) {\n   275â†’    const sessionTodoPath = join(\n   276â†’      homedir(),\n   277â†’      \".claude\",\n   278â†’      \"todos\",\n   279â†’      `${sessionId}.json`,\n   280â†’    );\n   281â†’    try {\n   282â†’      const data = readJsonFile(sessionTodoPath);\n   283â†’      const todos = Array.isArray(data)\n   284â†’        ? data\n   285â†’        : Array.isArray(data?.todos)\n   286â†’          ? data.todos\n   287â†’          : [];\n   288â†’      count += todos.filter(\n   289â†’        (t) => t.status !== \"completed\" && t.status !== \"cancelled\",\n   290â†’      ).length;\n   291â†’    } catch {\n   292â†’      /* skip */\n   293â†’    }\n   294â†’  }\n   295â†’\n   296â†’  // Project-local todos only\n   297â†’  for (const path of [\n   298â†’    join(projectDir, \".omc\", \"todos.json\"),\n   299â†’    join(projectDir, \".claude\", \"todos.json\"),\n   300â†’  ]) {\n   301â†’    try {\n   302â†’      const data = readJsonFile(path);\n   303â†’      const todos = Array.isArray(data)\n   304â†’        ? data\n   305â†’        : Array.isArray(data?.todos)\n   306â†’          ? data.todos\n   307â†’          : [];\n   308â†’      count += todos.filter(\n   309â†’        (t) => t.status !== \"completed\" && t.status !== \"cancelled\",\n   310â†’      ).length;\n   311â†’    } catch {\n   312â†’      /* skip */\n   313â†’    }\n   314â†’  }\n   315â†’\n   316â†’  return count;\n   317â†’}\n   318â†’\n   319â†’/**\n   320â†’ * Detect if stop was triggered by context-limit related reasons.\n   321â†’ * When context is exhausted, Claude Code needs to stop so it can compact.\n   322â†’ * Blocking these stops causes a deadlock: can't compact because can't stop,\n   323â†’ * can't continue because context is full.\n   324â†’ *\n   325â†’ * See: https://github.com/Yeachan-Heo/oh-my-claudecode/issues/213\n   326â†’ */\n   327â†’function isContextLimitStop(data) {\n   328â†’  const reason = (data.stop_reason || data.stopReason || \"\").toLowerCase();\n   329â†’\n   330â†’  const contextPatterns = [\n   331â†’    \"context_limit\",\n   332â†’    \"context_window\",\n   333â†’    \"context_exceeded\",\n   334â†’    \"context_full\",\n   335â†’    \"max_context\",\n   336â†’    \"token_limit\",\n   337â†’    \"max_tokens\",\n   338â†’    \"conversation_too_long\",\n   339â†’    \"input_too_long\",\n   340â†’  ];\n   341â†’\n   342â†’  if (contextPatterns.some((p) => reason.includes(p))) {\n   343â†’    return true;\n   344â†’  }\n   345â†’\n   346â†’  const endTurnReason = (\n   347â†’    data.end_turn_reason ||\n   348â†’    data.endTurnReason ||\n   349â†’    \"\"\n   350â†’  ).toLowerCase();\n   351â†’  if (endTurnReason && contextPatterns.some((p) => endTurnReason.includes(p))) {\n   352â†’    return true;\n   353â†’  }\n   354â†’\n   355â†’  return false;\n   356â†’}\n   357â†’\n   358â†’/**\n   359â†’ * Detect if stop was triggered by user abort (Ctrl+C, cancel button, etc.)\n   360â†’ */\n   361â†’function isUserAbort(data) {\n   362â†’  if (data.user_requested || data.userRequested) return true;\n   363â†’\n   364â†’  const reason = (data.stop_reason || data.stopReason || \"\").toLowerCase();\n   365â†’  // Exact-match patterns: short generic words that cause false positives with .includes()\n   366â†’  const exactPatterns = [\"aborted\", \"abort\", \"cancel\", \"interrupt\"];\n   367â†’  // Substring patterns: compound words safe for .includes() matching\n   368â†’  const substringPatterns = [\n   369â†’    \"user_cancel\",\n   370â†’    \"user_interrupt\",\n   371â†’    \"ctrl_c\",\n   372â†’    \"manual_stop\",\n   373â†’  ];\n   374â†’\n   375â†’  return (\n   376â†’    exactPatterns.some((p) => reason === p) ||\n   377â†’    substringPatterns.some((p) => reason.includes(p))\n   378â†’  );\n   379â†’}\n   380â†’\n   381â†’async function main() {\n   382â†’  try {\n   383â†’    const input = await readStdin();\n   384â†’ 448â†’    // Swarm uses swarm-summary.json (not swarm-state.json) + marker file\n   449â†’    const swarmMarker = existsSync(join(stateDir, \"swarm-active.marker\"));\n   450â†’    const swarmSummary      const toolError = readLastToolError(stateDir);\n   473â†’          const errorGuidance = getToolErrorRetryGuidance(toolError);\n   474â†’\n   475â†’          ralph.state.iteration = iteration + Provides comprehensive guidance for creating and implementing Claude Code plugin hooks with focus on advanced prompt-based hooks API.\n     4â†’version: 0.1.0\n     5â†’---\n     6â†’\n     7â†’# Hook Development for Claude Code Plugins\n     8â†’\n     9â†’## Overview\n    10â†’\n    11â†’Hooks are event-driven automation scripts that execute in response to Claude Code events. Use hooks to validate operations, enforce policies, add context, and integrate external tools into workflows.\n    12â†’\n    13â†’**Key capabilities:**\n    14â†’- Validate tool calls before execution (PreToolUse)\n    15â†’- React to tool results (PostToolUse)\n    16â†’- Enforce completion standards (Stop, SubagentStop)\n    17â†’- Load project context (SessionStart)\n    18â†’- Automate workflows across the development lifecycle\n    19â†’\n    20â†’## Hook Types\n    21â†’\n    22â†’### Prompt-Based Hooks (Recommended)\n    23â†’\n    24â†’Use LLM-driven decision making for context-aware validation:\n    25â†’\n    26â†’```json\n    27â†’{\n    28â†’  \"type\": \"prompt\",\n    29â†’  \"prompt\": \"Evaluate if this tool use is appropriate: $TOOL_INPUT\",\n    30â†’  \"timeout\": 30\n    31â†’}\n    32â†’```\n    33â†’\n    34â†’**Supported events:** Stop, SubagentStop, UserPromptSubmit, PreToolUse\n    35â†’\n    36â†’**Benefits:**\n    37â†’- Context-aware decisions based on natural language reasoning\n    38â†’- Flexible evaluation logic without bash scripting\n    39â†’- Better edge case handling\n    40â†’- Easier to maintain and extend\n    41â†’\n    42â†’### Command Hooks\n    43â†’\n    44â†’Execute bash commands for deterministic checks:\n    45â†’\n    46â†’```json\n    47â†’{\n    48â†’  \"type\": \"command\",\n    49â†’  \"command\": \"bash ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/scripts/validate.sh\",\n    50â†’  \"timeout\": 60\n    51â†’}\n    52â†’```\n    53â†’\n    54â†’**Use for:**\n    55â†’- Fast deterministic validations\n    56â†’- File system operations\n    57â†’- External tool integrations\n    58â†’- Performance-critical checks\n    59â†’\n    60â†’## Hook Configuration Formats\n    61â†’\n    62â†’### Plugin hooks.json Format\n    63â†’\n    64â†’**For plugin hooks** in `hooks/hooks.json`, use wrapper format:\n    65â†’\n    66â†’```json\n    67â†’{\n    68â†’  \"description\": \"Brief explanation of hooks (optional)\",\n    69â†’  \"hooks\": {\n    70â†’    \"PreToolUse\": [...],\n    71â†’    \"Stop\": [...],\n    72â†’    \"SessionStart\": [...]\n    73â†’  }\n    74â†’}\n    75â†’```\n    76â†’\n    77â†’**Key points:**\n    78â†’- `description` field is optional\n    79â†’- `hooks` field is required wrapper containing actual hook events\n    80â†’- This is the **plugin-specific format**\n    81â†’\n    82â†’**Example:**\n    83â†’```json\n    84â†’{\n    85â†’  \"description\": \"Validation hooks for code quality\",\n    86â†’  \"hooks\": {\n    87â†’    \"PreToolUse\": [\n    88â†’      {\n \"${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/hooks/validate.sh\"\n    94â†’          }\n    95â†’        ]\n    96â†’      }\n    97â†’    ]\n    98â†’  }\n    99â†’}\n   100â†’```\n   101â†’\n   102â†’### Settings Format (Direct)\n   103â†’\n   104â†’**For user settings** in `.claude/settings.json`, use direct format:\n   105â†’\n   106â†’```json\n   107â†’{\n   108â†’  \"PreToolUse\": [...],\n   109â†’  \"Stop\": [...],\n   110â†’  \"SessionStart\": [...]\n   111â†’}\n   112â†’```\n   113â†’\n   114â†’**Key points:**\n   115â†’- No wrapper - events directly at top level\n   116â†’- No description field\n   117â†’- This is the **settings format**\n   118â†’\n   119â†’**Important:** The examples below show the hook event structure that goes inside either format. For plugin hooks.json, wrap these in `{\"hooks\": {...}}`.\n   120â†’\n   121â†’## Hook Events\n   122â†’\n   123â†’### PreToolUse\n   124â†’\n   125â†’Execute before any tool runs. Use to approve, deny, or modify tool calls.\n   126â†’\n   127â†’**Example (prompt-based):**\n   128â†’```json\n   129â†’{\n   130â†’  \"PreToolUse\": [\n   131â†’    {\n   132â†’      \"matcher\": \"Write|Edit\",\n   133â†’      \"hooks\": [\n   134â†’        {\n   135â†’          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   136â†’          \"prompt\": \"Validate file write safety. Check: system paths, credentials, path traversal, sensitive content. Return 'approve' or 'deny'.\"\n   137â†’        }\n   138â†’      ]\n   139â†’    }\n   140â†’  ]\n   141â†’}\n   142â†’```\n   143â†’\n   144â†’**Output for PreToolUse:**\n   145â†’```json\n   146â†’{\n   147â†’  \"hookSpecificOutput\": {\n   148â†’    \"permissionDecision\": \"allow|deny|ask\",\n   149â†’    \"updatedInput\": {\"field\": \"modified_value\"}\n   150â†’  },\n   151â†’  \"systemMessage\": \"Explanation for Claude\"\n   152â†’}\n   153â†’```\n   154â†’\n   155â†’### PostToolUse\n   156â†’\n   157â†’Execute after tool completes. Use to react to results, provide feedback, or log.\n   158â†’\n   159â†’**Example:**\n   160â†’```json\n   161â†’{\n   162â†’  \"PostToolUse\": [\n   163â†’    {\n   164â†’      \"matcher\": \"Edit\",\n   165â†’      \"hooks\": [\n   166â†’        {\n   167â†’          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   168â†’          \"prompt\": \"Analyze edit result for potential issues: syntax errors, security vulnerabilities, breaking changes. Provide feedback.\"\n   169â†’        }\n   170â†’      ]\n   171â†’    }\n   172â†’  ]\n   173â†’}\n   174â†’```\n   175â†’\n   176â†’**Output behavior:**\n   177â†’- Exit 0: stdout shown in transcript\n   178â†’- Exit 2: stderr fed back to Claude\n   179â†’- systemMessage included in context\n   180â†’\n   181â†’### Stop\n   182â†’\n   183â†’Execute when main agent considers stopping. Use to validate completeness.\n   184â†’\n   185â†’**Example:**\n   186â†’```json\n   187â†’{\n   188â†’  \"Stop\": [\n   189â†’    {\n   190â†’      \"matcher\": \"*\",\n   191â†’      \"hooks\": [\n   192â†’        {\n   193â†’          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   194â†’          \"prompt\": \"Verify task completion: tests run, build succeeded, questions answered. Return 'approve' to stop or 'block' with reason to continue.\"\n   195â†’        }\n   196â†’      ]\n   197â†’    }\n   198â†’  ]\n   199â†’}\n   200â†’```\n   201â†’\n   202â†’**Decision output:**\n   203â†’```json\n   204â†’{\n   205â†’  \"decision\": \"approve|block\",\n   206â†’  \"reason\": \"Explanation\",\n   207â†’  \"systemMessage\": \"Additional context\"\n   208â†’}\n   209â†’```\n   210â†’\n   211â†’### SubagentStop\n   212â†’\n   213â†’Execute when subagent considers stopping. Use to ensure subagent completed its task.\n   214â†’\n   215â†’Similar to Stop hook, but for subagents.\n   216â†’\n   217â†’### UserPromptSubmit\n   218â†’\n   219â†’Execute when user submits a prompt. Use to add context, validate, or block prompts.\n   220â†’\n   221â†’**Example:**\n   222â†’```json\n   223â†’{\n   224â†’  \"UserPromptSubmit\": [\n   225â†’    {\n   226â†’      \"matcher\": \"*\",\n   227â†’      \"hooks\": [\n   228â†’        {\n   229â†’          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   230â†’          \"prompt\": \"Check if prompt requires security guidance. If discussing auth, permissions, or API security, return relevant warnings.\"\n   231â†’        }\n   232â†’      ]\n   233â†’    }\n   234â†’  ]\n   235â†’}\n   236â†’```\n   237â†’\n   238â†’### SessionStart\n   239â†’\n   240â†’Execute when Claude Code session begins. Use to load context and set environment.\n   241â†’\n   242â†’**Example:**\n   243â†’```json\n   244â†’{\n   245â†’  \"SessionStart\": [\n   246â†’    {\n   247â†’      \"matcher\": \"*\",\n   248â†’      \"hooks\": [\n   249â†’        {\n   250â†’          \"type\": \"command\",\n   251â†’          \"command\": \"bash ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/scripts/load-context.sh\"\n   252â†’        }\n   253â†’      ]\n   254â†’    }\n   255â†’  ]\n   256â†’}\n   257â†’```\n   258â†’\n   259â†’**Special capability:** Persist environment variables using `$CLAUDE_ENV_FILE`:\n   260â†’```bash\n   261â†’echo \"export PROJECT_TYPE=nodejs\" >> \"$CLAUDE_ENV_FILE\"\n   262â†’```\n   263â†’\n   264â†’See `examples/load-context.sh` for complete example.\n   265â†’\n   266â†’### SessionEnd\n   267â†’\n   268â†’Execute when session ends. Use for cleanup, logging, and state preservation.\n   269â†’\n   270â†’### PreCompact\n   271â†’\n   272â†’Execute before context compaction. Use to add critical information to preserve.\n   273â†’\n   274â†’### Notification\n   275â†’\n   276â†’Execute when Claude sends notifications. Use to react to user notifications.\n   277â†’\n   278â†’## Hook Output Format\n   279â†’\n   280â†’### Standard Output (All Hooks)\n   281â†’\n   282â†’```json\n   283â†’{\n   284â†’  \"continue\": true,\n   285â†’  \"suppressOutput\": false,\n   286â†’  \"systemMessage\": \"Message for Claude\"\n   287â†’}\n   288â†’```\n   289â†’\n   290â†’- `continue`: If false, halt processing (default true)\n   291â†’- `suppressOutput`: Hide output from transcript (default false)\n   292â†’- `systemMessage`: Message shown to Claude\n   293â†’\n   294â†’### Exit Codes\n   295â†’\n   296â†’- `0` - Success (stdout shown in transcript)\n   297â†’- `2` - Blocking error (stderr fed back to Claude)\n   298â†’- Other - Non-blocking error\n   299â†’\n   300â†’## Hook Input Format\n   301â†’\n   302â†’All hooks receive JSON via stdin with common fields:\n   303â†’\n   304â†’```json\n   305â†’{\n   306â†’  \"session_id\": \"abc123\",\n   307â†’  \"transcript_path\": \"/path/to/transcript.txt\",\n   308â†’  \"cwd\": \"/current/working/dir\",\n   309â†’  \"permission_mode\": \"ask|allow\",\n   310â†’  \"hook_event_name\": \"PreToolUse\"\n   311â†’}\n   312â†’```\n   313â†’\n   314â†’**Event-specific fields:**\n   315â†’\n   316â†’- **PreToolUse/PostToolUse:** `tool_name`, `tool_input`, `tool_result`\n   317â†’- **UserPromptSubmit:** `user_prompt`\n   318â†’- **Stop/SubagentStop:** `reason`\n   319â†’\n   320â†’Access fields in prompts using `$TOOL_INPUT`, `$TOOL_RESULT`, `$USER_PROMPT`, etc.\n   321â†’\n   322â†’## Environment Variables\n   323â†’\n   324â†’Available in all command hooks:\n   325â†’\n   326â†’- `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` - Project root path\n   327â†’- `$CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT` - Plugin directory (use for portable paths)\n   328â†’- `$CLAUDE_ENV_FILE` - SessionStart only: persist env vars here\n   329â†’- `$CLAUDE_CODE_REMOTE` - Set if running in remote context\n   330â†’\n   331â†’**Always use ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT} in hook commands for portability:**\n   332â†’\n   333â†’```json\n   334â†’{\n   335â†’  \"type\": \"command\",\n   336â†’  \"command\": \"bash ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/scripts/validate.sh\"\n   337â†’}\n   338â†’```\n   339â†’\n   340â†’## Plugin Hook Configuration\n   341â†’\n   342â†’In plugins, define hooks in `hooks/hooks.json`:\n   343â†’\n   344â†’```json\n   345â†’{\n   346â†’  \"PreToolUse\": [\n   347â†’    {\n   348â†’      \"matcher\": \"Write|Edit\",\n   349â†’      \"hooks\": [\n   350â†’        {\n   351â†’          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   352â†’          \"prompt\": \"Validate file write safety\"\n   353â†’        }\n   354â†’      ]\n   355â†’    }\n   356â†’  ],\n   357â†’  \"Stop\": [\n   358â†’    {\n   359â†’      \"matcher\": \"*\",\n   360â†’      \"hooks\": [\n   361â†’        {\n   362â†’          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   363â†’          \"prompt\": \"Verify task completion\"\n   364â†’        }\n   365â†’      ]\n   366â†’    }\n   367â†’  ],\n   368â†’  \"SessionStart\": [\n   369â†’    {\n   370â†’      \"matcher\": \"*\",\n   371â†’      \"hooks\": [\n   372â†’        {\n   373â†’          \"type\": \"command\",\n   374â†’          \"command\": \"bash ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/scripts/load-context.sh\",\n   375â†’          \"timeout\": 10\n   376â†’        }\n   377â†’      ]\n   378â†’    }\n   379â†’  ]\n   380â†’}\n   381â†’```\n   382â†’\n   383â†’Plugin hooks merge with user's hooks and run in parallel.\n   384â†’\n   385â†’## Matchers\n   386â†’\n   387â†’### Tool Name Matching\n   388â†’\n   389â†’**Exact match:**\n   390â†’```json\n   391â†’\"matcher\": \"Write\"\n   392â†’```\n   393â†’\n   394â†’**Multiple tools:**\n   395â†’```json\n   396â†’\"matcher\": \"Read|Write|Edit\"\n   397â†’```\n   398â†’\n   399â†’**Wildcard (all tools):**\n   400â†’```json\n   401â†’\"matcher\": \"*\"\n   402â†’```\n   403â†’\n   404â†’**Regex patterns:**\n   405â†’```json\n   406â†’\"matcher\": \"mcp__.*__delete.*\"  // All MCP delete tools\n   407â†’```\n   408â†’\n   409â†’**Note:** Matchers are case-sensitive.\n   410â†’\n   411â†’### Common Patterns\n   412â†’\n   413â†’```json\n   414â†’// All MCP tools\n   415â†’\"matcher\": \"mcp__.*\"\n   416â†’\n   417â†’// Specific plugin's MCP tools\n   418â†’\"matcher\": \"mcp__plugin_asana_.*\"\n   419â†’\n   420â†’// All file operations\n   421â†’\"matcher\": \"Read|Write|Edit\"\n   422â†’\n   423â†’// Bash commands only\n   424â†’\"matcher\": \"Bash\"\n   425â†’```\n   426â†’\n   427â†’## Security Best Practices\n   428â†’\n   429â†’### Input Validation\n   430â†’\n   431â†’Always validate inputs in command hooks:\n   432â†’\n   433â†’```bash\n   434â†’#!/bin/bash\n   435â†’set -euo pipefail\n   436â†’\n   437â†’input=$(cat)\n   438â†’tool_name=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_name')\n   439â†’\n   440â†’# Validate tool name format\n   441â†’if [[ ! \"$tool_name\" =~ ^[a-zA-Z0-9_]+$ ]]; then\n   442â†’  echo '{\"decision\": \"deny\", \"reason\": \"Invalid tool name\"}' >&2\n   443â†’  exit 2\n   444â†’fi\n   445â†’```\n   446â†’\n   447â†’### Path Safety\n   448â†’\n   449â†’Check for path traversal and sensitive files:\n   450â†’\n   451â†’```bash\n   452â†’file_path=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.file_path')\n   453â†’\n   454â†’# Deny path traversal\n   455â†’if [[ \"$file_path\" == *\"..\"* ]]; then\n   456â†’  echo '{\"decision\": \"deny\", \"reason\": \"Path traversal detected\"}' >&2\n   457â†’  exit 2\n   458â†’fi\n   459â†’\n   460â†’# Deny sensitive files\n   461â†’if [[ \"$file_path\" == *\".env\"* ]]; then\n   462â†’  echo '{\"decision\": \"deny\", \"reason\": \"Sensitive file\"}' >&2\n   463â†’  exit 2\n   464â†’fi\n   465â†’```\n   466â†’\n   467â†’See `examples/validate-write.sh` and `examples/validate-bash.sh` for complete examples.\n   468â†’\n   469â†’### Quote All Variables\n   470â†’\n   471â†’```bash\n   472â†’# GOOD: Quoted\n   473â†’echo \"$file_path\"\n   474â†’cd \"$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR\"\n   475â†’\n   476â†’# BAD: Unquoted (injection risk)\n   477â†’echo $file_path\n   478â†’cd $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR\n   479â†’```\n   480â†’\n   481â†’### Set Appropriate Timeouts\n   482â†’\n   483â†’```json\n   484â†’{\n   485â†’  \"type\": \"command\",\n   486â†’  \"command\": \"bash script.sh\",\n   487â†’  \"timeout\": 10\n   488â†’}\n   489â†’```\n   490â†’\n   491â†’**Defaults:** Command hooks (60s), Prompt hooks (30s)\n   492â†’\n   493â†’## Performance Considerations\n   494â†’\n   495â†’### Parallel Execution\n   496â†’\n   497â†’All matching hooks run **in parallel**:\n   498â†’\n   499â†’```json\n   500â†’{\n   501â†’  \"PreToolUse\": [\n   502â†’    {\n   503â†’      \"matcher\": \"Write\",\n   504â†’      \"hooks\": [\n   505â†’        {\"type\": \"command\", \"command\": \"check1.sh\"},  // Parallel\n   506â†’        {\"type\": \"command\", \"command\": \"check2.sh\"},  // Parallel\n   507â†’        {\"type\": \"prompt\", \"prompt\": \"Validate...\"}   // Parallel\n   508â†’      ]\n   509â†’    }\n   510â†’  ]\n   511â†’}\n   512â†’```\n   513â†’\n   514â†’**Design implications:**\n   515â†’- Hooks don't see each other's output\n   516â†’- Non-deterministic ordering\n   517â†’- Design for independence\n   518â†’\n   519â†’### Optimization\n   520â†’\n   521â†’1. Use command hooks for quick deterministic checks\n   522â†’2. Use prompt hooks for complex reasoning\n   523â†’3. Cache validation results in temp files\n   524â†’4. Minimize I/O in hot paths\n   525â†’\n   526â†’## Temporarily Active Hooks\n   527â†’\n   528â†’Create hooks that activate conditionally by checking for a flag file or configuration:\n   529â†’\n   530â†’**Pattern: Flag file activation**\n   531â†’```bash\n   532â†’#!/bin/bash\n   533â†’# Only active when flag file exists\n   534â†’FLAG_FILE=\"$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.enable-strict-validation\"\n   535â†’\n   536â†’if [ ! -f \"$FLAG_FILE\" ]; then\n   537â†’  # Flag not present, skip validation\n   538â†’  exit 0\n   539â†’fi\n   540â†’\n   541â†’# Flag present, run validation\n   542â†’input=$(cat)\n   543â†’# ... validation logic ...\n   544â†’```\n   545â†’\n   546â†’**Pattern: Configuration-based activation**\n   547â†’```bash\n   548â†’#!/bin/bash\n   549â†’# Check configuration for activation\n   550â†’CONFIG_FILE=\"$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.claude/plugin-config.json\"\n   551â†’\n   552â†’if [ -f \"$CONFIG_FILE\" ]; then\n   553â†’  enabled=$(jq -r '.strictMode // false' \"$CONFIG_FILE\")\n   554â†’  if [ \"$enabled\" != \"true\" ]; then\n   555â†’    exit 0  # Not enabled, skip\n   556â†’  fi\n   557â†’fi\n   558â†’\n   559â†’# Enabled, run hook logic\n   560â†’input=$(cat)\n   561â†’# ... hook logic ...\n   562â†’```\n   563â†’\n   564â†’**Use cases:**\n   565â†’- Enable strict validation only when needed\n   566â†’- Temporary debugging hooks\n   567â†’- Project-specific hook behavior\n   568â†’- Feature flags for hooks\n   569â†’\n   570â†’**Best practice:** Document activation mechanism in plugin README so users know how to enable/disable temporary hooks.\n   571â†’\n   572â†’## Hook Lifecycle and Limitations\n   573â†’\n   574â†’### Hooks Load at Session Start\n   575â†’\n   576â†’**Important:** Hooks are loaded when Claude Code session starts. Changes to hook configuration require restarting Claude Code.\n   577â†’\n   578â†’**Cannot hot-swap hooks:**\n   579â†’- Editing `hooks/hooks.json` won't affect current session\n   580â†’- Adding new hook scripts won't be recognized\n   581â†’- Changing hook commands/prompts won't update\n   582â†’- Must restart Claude Code: exit and run `claude` again\n   583â†’\n   584â†’**To test hook changes:**\n   585â†’1. Edit hook configuration or scripts\n   586â†’2. Exit Claude Code session\n   587â†’3. Restart: `claude` or `cc`\n   588â†’4. New hook configuration loads\n   589â†’5. Test hooks with `claude --debug`\n   590â†’\n   591â†’### Hook Validation at Startup\n   592â†’\n   593â†’Hooks are validated when Claude Code starts:\n   594â†’- Invalid JSON in hooks.json causes loading failure\n   595â†’- Missing scripts cause warnings\n   596â†’- Syntax errors reported in debug mode\n   597â†’\n   598â†’Use `/hooks` command to review loaded hooks in current session.\n   599â†’\n   600â†’## Debugging Hooks\n   601â†’\n   602â†’### Enable Debug Mode\n   603â†’\n   604â†’```bash\n   605â†’claude --debug\n   606â†’```\n   607â†’\n   608â†’Look for hook registration, 620â†’\n   621â†’### Validate JSON Output\n   622â†’\n   623â†’Ensure hooks output valid JSON:\n   624â†’\n   625â†’```bash\n   626â†’output=$(./your-hook.sh < test-input.json)\n   627â†’echo \"$output\" | jq .\n   628â†’```\n   629â†’\n   630â†’## Quick Reference\n   631â†’\n   632â†’### Hook Events Summary\n   633â†’\n   634â†’| Event | When | Use For |\n   635â†’|-------|------|---------|\n   636â†’| PreToolUse | Before tool | Validation, modification |\n   637â†’| PostToolUse | After tool | Feedback, logging |\n   638â†’| UserPromptSubmit | User input 645â†’\n   646â†’### Best Practices\n   647â†’\n   648â†’**DO:**\n   649â†’- âœ… Use prompt-based hooks for complex logic\n   650â†’- âœ… Use ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT} for portability\n   651â†’- âœ… Validate all inputs in command hooks\n   652â†’- âœ… Quote all bash variables\n   653â†’- âœ… Set appropriate timeouts\n   654â†’- âœ… Return structured JSON output\n   655â†’- âœ… Test hooks {"parentUuid":"693ce662-93c3-4359-bb47-916437f0870b","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"67fcde4a-7483-4526-a2da-9ae9514890c8","agentId":"afdb282d866e3c1e4","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01APicffe2GyyfWaB3cuUbDN","type":"tool_result","content":"     1â†’# Migrating from Basic to Advanced Hooks\n     2â†’\n     3â†’This guide shows how to migrate from basic command hooks to advanced prompt-based hooks for better maintainability and flexibility.\n     4â†’\n     5â†’## Why Migrate?\n     6â†’\n     7â†’Prompt-based hooks offer several advantages:\n     8â†’\n     9â†’- **Natural language reasoning**: LLM understands context and intent\n    10â†’- **Better edge case handling**: Adapts to unexpected scenarios\n    11â†’- **No bash scripting required**: Simpler to write and maintain\n    12â†’- **More flexible validation**: Can handle complex logic without coding\n    13â†’\n    14â†’## Migration Example: Bash Command Validation\n    15â†’\n    16â†’### Before (Basic Command Hook)\n    17â†’\n    18â†’**Configuration:**\n    19â†’```json\n    20â†’{\n    21â†’  \"PreToolUse\": [\n    22â†’    {\n    23â†’      \"matcher\": \"Bash\",\n    24â†’      \"hooks\": [\n    25â†’        {\n    26â†’          \"type\": \"command\",\n    27â†’          \"command\": \"bash validate-bash.sh\"\n    28â†’        }\n    29â†’      ]\n    30â†’    }\n    31â†’  ]\n    32â†’}\n    33â†’```\n    34â†’\n    35â†’**Script (validate-bash.sh):**\n    36â†’```bash\n    37â†’#!/bin/bash\n    38â†’input=$(cat)\n    39â†’command=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.command')\n    40â†’\n    41â†’# Hard-coded validation logic\n    42â†’if [[ \"$command\" == *\"rm -rf\"* ]]; then\n    43â†’  echo \"Dangerous command detected\" >&2\n    44â†’  exit 2\n    45â†’fi\n    46â†’```\n    47â†’\n    48â†’**Problems:**\n    49â†’- Only checks for exact \"rm -rf\" pattern\n    50â†’- Doesn't catch variations like `rm -fr` or `rm -r -f`\n    51â†’- Misses other dangerous commands (`dd`, `mkfs`, etc.)\n    52â†’- No context awareness\n    53â†’- Requires bash scripting knowledge\n    54â†’\n    55â†’### After (Advanced Prompt Hook)\n    56â†’\n    57â†’**Configuration:**\n    58â†’```json\n    59â†’{\n    60â†’  \"PreToolUse\": [\n    61â†’    {\n    62â†’      \"matcher\": \"Bash\",\n    63â†’      \"hooks\": [\n    64â†’        {\n    65â†’          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n    66â†’          \"prompt\": \"Command: $TOOL_INPUT.command. Analyze for: 1) Destructive operations (rm -rf, dd, mkfs, etc) 2) Privilege escalation (sudo) 3) Network operations without user consent. Return 'approve' or 'deny' with explanation.\",\n    67â†’          \"timeout\": 15\n    68â†’        }\n    69â†’      ]\n    70â†’    }\n    71â†’  ]\n    72â†’}\n    73â†’```\n    74â†’\n    75â†’**Benefits:**\n    76â†’- Catches all variations and patterns\n    77â†’- Understands intent, not just literal strings\n    78â†’- No script file needed\n    79â†’- Easy to extend with new criteria\n    80â†’- Context-aware decisions\n    81â†’- Natural language explanation in denial\n    82â†’\n    83â†’## Migration Example: File Write Validation\n    84â†’\n    85â†’### Before (Basic Command Hook)\n    86â†’\n    87â†’**Configuration:**\n    88â†’```json\n    89â†’{\n    90â†’  \"PreToolUse\": [\n    91â†’    {\n    92â†’      \"matcher\": \"Write\",\n    93â†’      \"hooks\": [\n    94â†’        {\n    95â†’          \"type\": \"command\",\n    96â†’          \"command\": \"bash validate-write.sh\"\n    97â†’        }\n    98â†’      ]\n    99â†’    }\n   100â†’  ]\n   101â†’}\n   102â†’```\n   103â†’\n   104â†’**Script (validate-write.sh):**\n   105â†’```bash\n   106â†’#!/bin/bash\n   107â†’input=$(cat)\n   108â†’file_path=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.file_path')\n   109â†’\n   110â†’# Check for path traversal\n   111â†’if [[ \"$file_path\" == *\"..\"* ]]; then\n   112â†’  echo '{\"decision\": \"deny\", \"reason\": \"Path traversal detected\"}' >&2\n   113â†’  exit 2\n   114â†’fi\n   115â†’\n   116â†’# Check for system paths\n   117â†’if [[ \"$file_path\" == \"/etc/\"* ]] || [[ \"$file_path\" == \"/sys/\"* ]]; then\n   118â†’  echo '{\"decision\": \"deny\", \"reason\": \"System file\"}' >&2\n   119â†’  exit 2\n   120â†’fi\n   121â†’```\n   122â†’\n   123â†’**Problems:**\n   124â†’- Hard-coded path patterns\n   125â†’- Doesn't understand symlinks\n   126â†’- Missing edge cases (e.g., `/etc` vs `/etc/`)\n   127â†’- No consideration of file content\n   128â†’\n   129â†’### After (Advanced Prompt Hook)\n   130â†’\n   131â†’**Configuration:**\n   132â†’```json\n   133â†’{\n   134â†’  \"PreToolUse\": [\n   135â†’    {\n   136â†’      \"matcher\": \"Write|Edit\",\n   137â†’      \"hooks\": [\n   138â†’        {\n   139â†’          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   140â†’          \"prompt\": \"File path: $TOOL_INPUT.file_path. Content preview: $TOOL_INPUT.content (first 200 chars). Verify: 1) Not system directories (/etc, /sys, /usr) 2) Not credentials (.env, tokens, secrets) 3) No path traversal 4) Content doesn't expose secrets. Return 'approve' or 'deny'.\"\n   141â†’        }\n   142â†’      ]\n   143â†’    }\n   144â†’  ]\n   145â†’}\n   146â†’```\n   147â†’\n   148â†’**Benefits:**\n   149â†’- Context-aware (considers content too)\n   150â†’- Handles symlinks and edge cases\n   151â†’- Natural understanding of \"system directories\"\n   152â†’- Can detect secrets in content\n   153â†’- Easy to extend criteria\n   154â†’\n   155â†’## When to Keep Command Hooks\n   156â†’\n   157â†’Command hooks still have their place:\n   158â†’\n   159â†’### 1. Deterministic Performance Checks\n   160â†’\n   161â†’```bash\n   162â†’#!/bin/bash\n   163â†’# Check file size quickly\n   164â†’file_path=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.file_path')\n   165â†’size=$(stat -f%z \"$file_path\" 2>/dev/null || stat -c%s \"$file_path\" 2>/dev/null)\n   166â†’\n   167â†’if [ \"$size\" -gt 10000000 ]; then\n   168â†’  echo '{\"decision\": \"deny\", \"reason\": \"File too large\"}' >&2\n   169â†’  exit 2\n   170â†’fi\n   171â†’```\n   172â†’\n   173â†’**Use command hooks when:** Validation is purely mathematical or deterministic.\n   174â†’\n   175â†’### 2. External Tool Integration\n   176â†’\n   177â†’```bash\n   178â†’#!/bin/bash\n   179â†’# Run security scanner\n   180â†’file_path=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.file_path')\n   181â†’scan_result=$(security-scanner \"$file_path\")\n   182â†’\n   183â†’if [ \"$?\" -ne 0 ]; then\n   184â†’  echo \"Security scan failed: $scan_result\" >&2\n   185â†’  exit 2\n   186â†’fi\n   187â†’```\n   188â†’\n   189â†’**Use command hooks when:** Integrating with external tools that provide yes/no answers.\n   190â†’\n   191â†’### 3. Very Fast Checks (< 50ms)\n   192â†’\n   193â†’```bash\n   194â†’#!/bin/bash\n   195â†’# Quick regex check\n   196â†’command=$(echo \"$input\" | jq -r '.tool_input.command')\n   197â†’\n   198â†’if [[ \"$command\" =~ ^(ls|pwd|echo)$ ]]; then\n   199â†’  exit 0  # Safe commands\n   200â†’fi\n   201â†’```\n   202â†’\n   203â†’**Use command hooks when:** Performance is critical and logic is simple.\n   204â†’\n   205â†’## Hybrid Approach\n   206â†’\n   207â†’Combine both for multi-stage validation:\n   208â†’\n   209â†’```json\n   210â†’{\n   211â†’  \"PreToolUse\": [\n   212â†’    {\n   213â†’      \"matcher\": \"Bash\",\n   214â†’      \"hooks\": [\n   215â†’        {\n   216â†’          \"type\": \"command\",\n   217â†’          \"command\": \"bash ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/scripts/quick-check.sh\",\n   218â†’          \"timeout\": 5\n   219â†’        },\n   220â†’        {\n   221â†’          \"type\": \"prompt\",\n   222â†’          \"prompt\": \"Deep analysis of bash command: $TOOL_INPUT\",\n   223â†’          \"timeout\": 15\n   224â†’        }\n   225â†’      ]\n   226â†’    }\n   227â†’  ]\n   228â†’}\n   229â†’```\n   230â†’\n   231â†’The command hook does fast deterministic checks, while the prompt hook handles complex reasoning.\n   232â†’\n   233â†’## Migration Checklist\n   234â†’\n   235â†’When migrating hooks:\n   236â†’\n   237â†’- [ ] Identify the validation logic in the command hook\n   238â†’- [ ] Convert hard-coded patterns to natural language criteria\n   239â†’- [ ] Test with edge cases the old hook missed\n   240â†’- [ ] Verify LLM understands the intent\n   241â†’- [ ] Set appropriate timeout (usually 15-30s for prompt hooks)\n   242â†’- [ ] Document the new hook in README\n   243â†’- [ ] Remove or archive old script files\n   244â†’\n   245â†’## Migration Tips\n   246â†’\n   247â†’1. **Start with one hook**: Don't migrate everything at once\n   248â†’2. **Test thoroughly**: Verify prompt hook catches what command hook caught\n   249â†’3. **Look for improvements**: Use migration as opportunity to enhance validation\n   250â†’4. **Keep scripts for reference**: Archive old scripts in case you need to reference the logic\n   251â†’5. **Document reasoning**: Explain why prompt hook is better in README\n   252â†’\n   253â†’## Complete Migration Example\n   254â†’\n   255â†’### Original Plugin Structure\n   256â†’\n   257â†’```\n   258â†’my-plugin/\n   259â†’â”œâ”€â”€ .claude-plugin/plugin.json\n   260â†’â”œâ”€â”€ hooks/hooks.json\n   261â†’â””â”€â”€ scripts/\n   262â†’ {"parentUuid":"6315aef9-abab-40e2-9c09-93b8684ce154","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"afdb282d866e3c1e4","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_01JwPjSGPtbHJfBUEti28bhR","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"\n\nI now have a complete picture. Let me compile everything into the guide.\n\n---\n\n## Complete Guide to Building a Stop Hook That Blocks Completion Until Pipeline Is Done\n\n### 1. The Stop Hook Protocol (How Claude Code Processes It)\n\nWhen Claude's main agent decides to stop, Claude Code fires every registered `Stop` hook. The hook receives JSON on **stdin** with these fields:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"session_id\": \"abc123\",\n  \"transcript_path\": \"/path/to/transcript.jsonl\",\n  \"cwd\": \"/current/working/dir\",\n  \"hook_event_name\": \"Stop\",\n  \"reason\": \"...\",\n  \"stop_reason\": \"...\",\n  \"end_turn_reason\": \"...\"\n}\n```\n\nThe hook's **stdout** JSON determines what happens:\n\n| Output | Effect |\n|--------|--------|\n| `{\"decision\": \"block\", \"reason\": \"...\"}` | **Agent cannot stop.** The `reason` string is injected as the next user message, forcing the agent to continue. |\n| `{\"decision\": \"approve\"}` or `{}` or exit 0 with no JSON | Agent stops normally. |\n| `{\"continue\": true, \"suppressOutput\": true}` | Allow stop, produce no visible output. |\n\nThe `reason` field is the critical mechanism: whatever text you put there becomes what Claude sees as its next instruction. This is how ralph-loop re-injects the same prompt every iteration.\n\nOptional additional field: `\"systemMessage\"` -- injected as a system-level context message alongside the reason.\n\n### 2. How ralph-loop Detects When to Block vs Allow\n\nThe ralph-loop plugin (`/Users/mohamedabdallah/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/claude-plugins-official/plugins/ralph-loop/hooks/stop-hook.sh`) uses a **state file sentinel** pattern. The decision tree:\n\n```\nState file .claude/ralph-loop.local.md exists?\n  NO  --> exit 0 (allow stop, no active loop)\n  YES --> Parse YAML frontmatter:\n    Session ID matches? (see section 3)\n      NO  --> exit 0 (not our session)\n      YES --> Numeric fields valid?\n        NO  --> rm state file, exit 0 (corrupted, bail safely)\n        YES --> max_iterations reached?\n          YES --> rm state file, exit 0 (done)\n          NO  --> Transcript readable?\n            NO  --> rm state file, exit 0 (broken, bail)\n            YES --> completion_promise set AND <promise>TEXT</promise> found in last assistant output?\n              YES --> rm state file, exit 0 (task complete)\n              NO  --> OUTPUT {\"decision\": \"block\", \"reason\": \"$PROMPT_TEXT\"}\n```\n\nKey design principle: **Every single error path allows the stop.** The hook never blocks on failure. It only blocks when it has confidently determined the loop should continue.\n\n### 3. How ralph-loop Tracks State Across Invocations\n\nState is a **markdown file with YAML frontmatter** at `.claude/ralph-loop.local.md`:\n\n```markdown\n---\nactive: true\niteration: 1\nsession_id: ${CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID}\nmax_iterations: 20\ncompletion_promise: \"TASK COMPLETE\"\nstarted_at: \"2026-03-20T10:00:00Z\"\n---\n\nThe actual prompt text goes here after the frontmatter.\n```\n\nOn each block:\n1. Read iteration count from frontmatter\n2. Increment: `sed \"s/^iteration: .*/iteration: $NEXT_ITERATION/\"`\n3. Atomic write: write to temp file (`${RALPH_STATE_FILE}.tmp.$$`), then `mv` to replace\n4. Extract prompt text (everything after the closing `---`)\n5. Emit `{\"decision\": \"block\", \"reason\": \"$PROMPT_TEXT\"}`\n\nThe OMC persistent-mode (`/Users/mohamedabdallah/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/omc/scripts/persistent-mode.mjs`) uses a different approach: **JSON state files** per mode (`ralph-state.json`, `ultrawork-state.json`, `pipeline-state.json`, etc.) stored in `.omc/state/` with fields like `active`, `iteration`, `reinforcement_count`, `last_checked_at`, `session_id`, `project_path`.\n\n### 4. How Session Isolation Works\n\n**ralph-loop approach** (simple, effective):\n```bash\n# Setup writes session ID into state file:\nsession_id: ${CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID:-}\n\n# Stop hook compares:\nSTATE_SESSION=$(grep '^session_id:' state_file)\nHOOK_SESSION=$(echo \"$HOOK_INPUT\" | jq -r '.session_id // \"\"')\nif [[ -n \"$STATE_SESSION\" ]] && [[ \"$STATE_SESSION\" != \"$HOOK_SESSION\" ]]; then\n  exit 0  # Not our session, allow stop\nfi\n```\n\nLegacy state files without `session_id` fall through (backwards compatibility).\n\n**OMC approach** (enterprise-grade):\n- Session-scoped state directories: `.omc/state/sessions/<sessionId>/<mode>-state.json`\n- Session ID validated with allowlist regex: `^[a-zA-Z0-9][a-zA-Z0-9_-]{0,255}$`\n- Project isolation: state file contains `project_path`, compared via normalized paths\n- Staleness threshold: states older than 2 hours are treated as inactive (prevents stale state from blocking new sessions)\n- If `session_id` field exists in state, it MUST match. If absent (legacy), allow.\n\n### 5. How the \"reason\" Field Re-injects Prompts\n\nThis is the core mechanism that makes Stop hooks powerful:\n\n**ralph-loop**: Extracts the prompt verbatim from the state file body (everything after YAML frontmatter) and puts it in `reason`. Also adds a `systemMessage` with iteration count and completion instructions:\n\n```bash\njq -n \\\n  --arg prompt \"$PROMPT_TEXT\" \\\n  --arg msg \"Ralph iteration $NEXT_ITERATION | To stop: output <promise>DONE</promise>\" \\\n  '{\"decision\": \"block\", \"reason\": $prompt, \"systemMessage\": $msg}'\n```\n\n**OMC persistent-mode**: Constructs a status-aware reason string:\n```javascript\nreason = `[PIPELINE - Stage ${currentStage + 1}/${totalStages}] Pipeline not complete. Continue working.`\n```\n\n**OMC context-guard-stop**: Uses reason as a warning:\n```javascript\nreason: `[OMC] Context at ${pct}% (threshold: ${THRESHOLD}%). Quality degrades at high context. Run /compact.`\n```\n\n**OMC code-simplifier**: Uses reason as a delegation instruction:\n```javascript\nreason: `[CODE SIMPLIFIER] Recently modified files detected. Delegate to the code-simplifier agent...`\n```\n\n**hookify rule_engine.py**: Uses combined rule messages as the reason:\n```python\nreturn {\"decision\": \"block\", \"reason\": combined_message, \"systemMessage\": combined_message}\n```\n\n### 6. Edge Case Handling (Comprehensive Catalog from All Implementations)\n\n#### Corrupted State (ralph-loop)\n```bash\nif [[ ! \"$ITERATION\" =~ ^[0-9]+$ ]]; then\n  echo \"State file corrupted\" >&2\n  rm \"$RALPH_STATE_FILE\"\n  exit 0  # Allow stop, never block on bad data\nfi\n```\n\nSame pattern for `MAX_ITERATIONS`, empty prompt text, missing transcript, unparseable JSON.\n\n**Universal rule: Every corruption path deletes state and allows stop.**\n\n#### Wrong Session (ralph-loop + OMC)\nBoth implementations silently allow the stop. No error, no warning. The hook simply is not active for this session.\n\n#### Context Limit / Compaction Deadlock (OMC -- critical)\n```javascript\nfunction isContextLimitStop(data) {\n  const reason = (data.stop_reason || '').toLowerCase();\n  const patterns = ['context_limit', 'context_window', 'token_limit', 'max_tokens', ...];\n  return patterns.some(p => reason.includes(p));\n}\n// CRITICAL: Never block context-limit stops\nif (isContextLimitStop(data)) {\n  console.log(JSON.stringify({ continue: true, suppressOutput: true }));\n  return;\n}\n```\n\nIf you block a context-limit stop, Claude Code cannot compact, and the session deadlocks. This is the **single most important edge case** to handle.\n\n#### User Abort / Ctrl+C (OMC)\n```javascript\nfunction isUserAbort(data) {\n  if (data.user_requested || data.userRequested) return true;\n  const reason = (data.stop_reason || '').toLowerCase();\n  return ['aborted', 'abort', 'cancel', 'interrupt'].some(p => reason === p) ||\n         ['user_cancel', 'ctrl_c', 'manual_stop'].some(p => reason.includes(p));\n}\n```\n\n**Never block user-initiated stops.** The user must always be able to escape.\n\n#### Retry Guard / Infinite Loop Prevention (OMC context-guard)\n```javascript\nconst MAX_BLOCKS = 2;\nfunction getBlockCount(sessionId) {\n  const guardFile = join(tmpdir(), `omc-context-guard-${sessionId}.json`);\n  // ... read from temp file ...\n}\n// After MAX_BLOCKS, stop blocking\nif (blockCount >= MAX_BLOCKS) {\n  console.log(JSON.stringify({ continue: true }));\n  return;\n}\n```\n\n**Cap the number of times you block.** Prevents infinite block loops.\n\n#### Max Reinforcements / Auto-Extension (OMC persistent-mode)\nRalph mode in OMC auto-extends when max iterations hit:\n```javascript\nif (iteration >= maxIter) {\n  ralph.state.max_iterations = maxIter + 10;\n  // block and continue\n}\n```\n\nUltrawork has `max_reinforcements` (default 50) -- when reached, allows stop.\n\n#### Staleness (OMC)\n```javascript\nconst STALE_STATE_THRESHOLD_MS = 2 * 60 * 60 * 1000; // 2 hours\nfunction isStaleState(state) {\n  const mostRecent = Math.max(last_checked_at, started_at);\n  return (Date.now() - mostRecent) > STALE_STATE_THRESHOLD_MS;\n}\n```\n\nPrevents stale state from a previous session from blocking a new one.\n\n#### Tool Error Recovery (OMC)\nReads `last-tool-error.json` (written by PostToolUse hooks) and prepends retry guidance to the reason. After 5+ retries, suggests alternative approaches instead of retrying.\n\n#### One-Shot Trigger Guard (OMC code-simplifier)\nUses a marker file to ensure it only blocks once per stop cycle:\n```javascript\nconst markerPath = join(stateDir, 'code-simplifier-triggered.marker');\nif (existsSync(markerPath)) {\n  unlinkSync(markerPath);  // Clear marker\n  // Allow stop (already triggered once)\n  return;\n}\nwriteFileSync(markerPath, new Date().toISOString());\n// Block and delegate\n```\n\n#### Safety Timeout (OMC code-simplifier)\n```javascript\nconst safetyTimeout = setTimeout(() => {\n  process.stdout.write(JSON.stringify({ continue: true }) + '\\n');\n  process.exit(0);\n}, 10000);\n```\n\nForces exit after 10 seconds even if the hook hangs. **A hanging hook is worse than a missing hook.**\n\n#### Stdin Timeout (OMC shared lib)\n```javascript\nexport async function readStdin(timeoutMs = 5000) {\n  // ... event-based reading with timeout safety net ...\n  // On Linux/Windows, stdin can hang indefinitely if parent doesn't close it\n}\n```\n\n#### Global Error Handlers (OMC)\n```javascript\nprocess.on('uncaughtException', () => {\n  process.stdout.write(JSON.stringify({ continue: true }) + '\\n');\n  process.exit(0);\n});\nprocess.on('unhandledRejection', () => { /* same */ });\n```\n\n**On ANY unhandled error, allow the stop.** Never block by accident.\n\n### 7. Complete Inventory of Stop Hook Implementations Found\n\n| Plugin | File | Language | Block Mechanism |\n|--------|------|----------|-----------------|\n| **ralph-loop** | `hooks/stop-hook.sh` | Bash | State file sentinel + prompt re-injection |\n| **hookify** | `hooks/stop.py` + `core/rule_engine.py` | Python | User-defined rules from `.local.md` config files |\n| **OMC context-guard** | `scripts/context-guard-stop.mjs` | Node.js | Context % threshold with retry cap |\n| **OMC persistent-mode** | `scripts/persistent-mode.mjs` (.cjs at runtime) | Node.js | Multi-mode state machine (ralph/autopilot/ultrapilot/swarm/pipeline/ultraqa/ultrawork) |\n| **OMC code-simplifier** | `scripts/code-simplifier.mjs` | Node.js | One-shot delegation trigger with marker file |\n| **Wazir** | `hooks/stop-handoff-harvest` | Node.js | Currently **does not block** -- only harvests observability data |\n| **plugin-dev** (reference) | `skills/hook-development/SKILL.md` | Docs | Prompt-based Stop hook examples |\n\n### 8. Blueprint: Wazir Pipeline Stop Hook\n\nBased on everything above, here is the architecture for a Stop hook that blocks until the Wazir pipeline is done.\n\n**hooks.json registration:**\n```json\n{\n  \"Stop\": [\n    {\n      \"hooks\": [\n        {\n          \"type\": \"command\",\n          \"command\": \"./hooks/pipeline-gate\",\n          \"timeout\": 10\n        }\n      ]\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n**Decision logic (pipeline-gate script):**\n\n```\n1. Read stdin (with timeout -- never hang)\n2. Parse JSON input\n3. SAFETY FIRST:\n   a. Is this a context_limit stop? --> allow (prevent compaction deadlock)\n   b. Is this a user abort? --> allow (respect Ctrl+C)\n4. Read pipeline-state.json from ~/.wazir/projects/<slug>/\n   a. Not found? --> allow (no active pipeline)\n   b. JSON parse error? --> allow + warn stderr\n5. SESSION ISOLATION:\n   a. State has session_id AND it doesn't match input session_id? --> allow\n6. STALENESS:\n   a. State last_checked_at older than 2 hours? --> allow\n7. RETRY GUARD:\n   a. reinforcement_count > max_reinforcements? --> allow\n8. PIPELINE CHECK:\n   a. Is current_phase === \"complete\"? --> allow\n   b. Are all required proof artifacts present? --> allow\n   c. Otherwise: BLOCK with reason describing what's missing\n9. UPDATE STATE:\n   a. Increment reinforcement_count\n   b. Update last_checked_at\n   c. Write state atomically (temp file + rename)\n10. OUTPUT: {\"decision\": \"block\", \"reason\": \"...\", \"systemMessage\": \"...\"}\n11. On ANY uncaught error: allow stop, write to stderr\n```\n\n**Key design principles distilled from all implementations:**\n\n1. **Never block on error.** Every catch/finally exits 0 and allows the stop.\n2. **Never block context-limit stops.** Causes compaction deadlock.\n3. **Never block user aborts.** The human is always in control.\n4. **Session isolation is mandatory.** Multiple sessions in the same project must not interfere.\n5. **Staleness detection prevents ghost blocks.** Old state from crashed sessions must not persist.\n6. **Retry guards prevent infinite loops.** Cap the maximum number of blocks.\n7. **Atomic state writes.** Temp file + rename, never in-place overwrites.\n8. **Command hooks only, never prompt hooks** for enforcement. Prompt hooks re-introduce the rationalization problem (the agent can talk itself into approving its own stop).\n9. **The `reason` field is your control channel.** Put actionable instructions there -- what's missing, what to do next.\n10. **stdin can hang.** Use timeout-protected reading (5s default)."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":614,"cache_read_input_tokens":92354,"output_tokens":4008,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":614},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZERU91MY3FnQsvn6ehsb","type":"assistant","uuid":"4d9a298f-69db-44ca-a083-0ab3d76d3d11","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:38:44.229Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}
